/// Provider for `query mir_borrowck`. Similar to `typeck`, this must\n115: /// only be called for typeck roots which will then borrowck all\n116: /// nested bodies as well.\n117: fn mir_borrowck(\n118:     tcx: TyCtxt<'_>,\n119:     def: LocalDefId,\n120: ) -> Result<&FxIndexMap<LocalDefId, ty::DefinitionSiteHiddenType<'_>>, ErrorGuaranteed> {\n121:     assert!(!tcx.is_typeck_child(def.to_def_id()));\n122:     let (input_body, _) = tcx.mir_promoted(def);\n123:     debug!(\"run query mir_borrowck: {}\", tcx.def_path_str(def));\n124: \n125:     let input_body: &Body<'_> = &input_body.borrow();\n126:     if let Some(guar) = input_body.tainted_by_errors {\n127:         debug!(\"Skipping borrowck because of tainted body\");\n128:         Err(guar)\n129:     } else if input_body.should_skip() {\n130:         debug!(\"Skipping borrowck because of injected body\");\n131:         let opaque_types = Default::default();\n132:         Ok(tcx.arena.alloc(opaque_types))\n133:     } else {\n134:         let mut root_cx = BorrowCheckRootCtxt::new(tcx, def, None);\n135:         root_cx.do_mir_borrowck();\n136:         root_cx.finalize()\n137:     }\n138: }\n139: \n140: /// Data propagated to the typeck parent by nested items.\n141: /// This should always be empty for the typeck root.\n142: #[derive(Debug)]\n143: struct PropagatedBorrowCheckResults<'tcx> {\n144:     closure_requirements: Option<ClosureRegionRequirements<'tcx>>,\n145:     used_mut_upvars: SmallVec<[FieldIdx; 8]>,\n146: }\n147: \n148: type DeferredClosureRequirements<'tcx> = Vec<(LocalDefId, ty::GenericArgsRef<'tcx>, Locations)>;\n149: \n150: /// After we borrow check a closure, we are left with various\n151: /// requirements that we have inferred between the free regions that\n152: /// appear in the closure's signature or on its field types. These\n153: /// requirements are then verified and proved by the closure's\n154: /// creating function. This struct encodes those requirements.\n155: ///\n156: /// The requirements are listed as being between various `RegionVid`. The 0th\n157: /// region refers to `'static`; subsequent region vids refer to the free\n158: /// regions that appear in the closure (or coroutine's) type, in order of\n159: /// appearance. (This numbering is actually defined by the `UniversalRegions`\n160: /// struct in the NLL region checker. See for example\n161: /// `UniversalRegions::closure_mapping`.) Note the free regions in the\n162: /// closure's signature and captures are erased.\n163: ///\n164: /// Example: If type check produces a closure with the closure args:\n165: ///\n166: /// ```text\n167: /// ClosureArgs = [\n168: ///     'a,                                         // From the parent.\n169: ///     'b,\n170: ///     i8,                                         // the \"closure kind\"\n171: ///     for<'x> fn(&'<erased> &'x u32) -> &'x u32,  // the \"closure signature\"\n172: ///     &'<erased> String,                          // some upvar\n173: /// ]\n174: /// ```\n175: ///\n176: /// We would \"renumber\" each free region to a unique vid, as follows:\n177: ///\n178: /// ```text\n179: /// ClosureArgs = [\n180: ///     '1,                                         // From the parent.\n181: ///     '2,\n182: ///     i8,                                         // the \"closure kind\"\n183: ///     for<'x> fn(&'3 &'x u32) -> &'x u32,         // the \"closure signature\"\n184: ///     &'4 String,                                 // some upvar\n185: /// ]\n186: /// ```\n187: ///\n188: /// Now the code might impose a requirement like `'1: '2`. When an\n189: /// instance of the closure is created, the corresponding free regions\n190: /// can be extracted from its type and constrained to have the given\n191: /// outlives relationship.\n192: #[derive(Clone, Debug)]\n193: pub struct ClosureRegionRequirements<'tcx> {\n194:     /// The number of external regions defined on the closure. In our\n195:     /// example above, it would be 3 -- one for `'static`, then `'1`\n196:     /// and `'2`. This is just used for a sanity check later on, to\n197:     /// make sure that the number of regions we see at the callsite\n198:     /// matches.\n199:     pub num_external_vids: usize,\n200: \n201:     /// Requirements between the various free regions defined in\n202:     /// indices.\n203:     pub outlives_requirements: Vec<ClosureOutlivesRequirement<'tcx>>,\n204: }\n205: \n206: /// Indicates an outlives-constraint between a type or between two\n207: /// free regions declared on the closure.\n208: #[derive(Copy, Clone, Debug)]\n209: pub struct ClosureOutlivesRequirement<'tcx> {\n210:     // This region or type ...\n211:     pub subject: ClosureOutlivesSubject<'tcx>,\n212: \n213:     // ... must outlive this one.\n214:     pub outlived_free_region: ty::RegionVid,\n215: \n216:     // If not, report an error here ...\n217:     pub blame_span: Span,\n218: \n219:     // ... due to this reason.\n220:     pub category: ConstraintCategory<'tcx>,\n221: }\n222: \n223: // Make sure this enum doesn't unintentionally grow\n224: #[cfg(target_pointer_width = \"64\")]\n225: rustc_data_structures::static_assert_size!(ConstraintCategory<'_>, 16);\n226: \n227: /// The subject of a `ClosureOutlivesRequirement` -- that is, the thing\n228: /// that must outlive some region.\n229: #[derive(Copy, Clone, Debug)]\n230: pub enum ClosureOutlivesSubject<'tcx> {\n231:     /// Subject is a type, typically a type parameter, but could also\n232:     /// be a projection. Indicates a requirement like `T: 'a` being\n233:     /// passed to the caller, where the type here is `T`.\n234:     Ty(ClosureOutlivesSubjectTy<'tcx>),\n235: \n236:     /// Subject is a free region from the closure.  /// universal regions *external* to the closure.\n258:     pub fn bind(tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>, ty: Ty<'tcx>) -> Self {\n259:         let inner = fold_regions(tcx, ty, |r, depth| match r.kind() {\n260: MirBorrowckCtxt<'a, '_, 'tcx> {\n787:     fn visit_after_early_statement_effect(\n788:         &mut self,\n789:         _analysis: &Borrowck<'a, 'tcx>,\n790:         state: &BorrowckDomain,\n791:         stmt: &Statement<'tcx>,\n792:         location: Location,\n793:     ) {\n794:         debug!(\"MirBorrowckCtxt::process_statement({:?}, {:?}): {:?}\", location, stmt, state);\n795:         let span                self.consume_rvalue(location, (rhs, span), state);\n802: \n803:                 self.mutate_place(location, (*lhs, span), Shallow(None), state);\n804:             }\n805:             StatementKind::FakeRead(box (_, place)) => {\n806:                 // Read for match doesn't access any memory and is used to\n807:                 // assert that a place is safe and live. StatementKind::Intrinsic(box kind) => match kind {\n824:                 NonDivergingIntrinsic::Assume(op) => {\n825:                     self.consume_operand(location, (op, span), state);\n826:                 }\n827:                 NonDivergingIntrinsic::CopyNonOverlapping(..) => span_bug!(\n828:                     span,\n829:                     \"Unexpected CopyNonOverlapping, should only visit_after_primary_terminator_effect(\n983:         &mut self,\n984:         _analysis: &Borrowck<'a, 'tcx>,\n985:         state: &BorrowckDomain,\n986:         term: &Terminator<'tcx>,\n987:              let borrow = &self.borrow_set[i];\n997:                         self.check_for_local_borrow(borrow, span);\n998:                     }\n999:                 }\n1000:             }\n1001: }\n1035: }\n1036: \n1037: use self::AccessDepth::{Deep, Shallow};\n1038: use self::ReadOrWrite::{Activation, Read, Reservation, Write};\n1039: \n1040: #[derive(Copy, Clone, PartialEq, Eq, Debug)]\n1041: enum ArtificialField {\n1042:     ArrayLength,\n1043:     FakeBorrow,\n1044: }\n1045: \n1046: #[derive(Copy, Clone, PartialEq, Eq, Debug)]\n1047: enum AccessDepth {\n1048:     /// From the RFC: \"A *shallow* access means that the immediate\n1049:     /// fields reached at P are accessed, but references or pointers\n1050:     /// found within are not dereferenced. Right now, the only access\n1051:     /// that is shallow is an assignment like `x = ...;`, which would\n1052:     /// be a *shallow write* of `x`.\"\n1053:     Shallow(Option<ArtificialField>),\n1054: \n1055:     /// From the RFC: \"A *deep* access means that all data reachable\n1056:     /// through the given place may be invalidated or accesses by\n1057:     /// this action.\"\n1058:     Deep,\n1059: \n1060:     /// Access is Deep only when there is a Drop implementation that\n1061:     /// can reach the data behind the reference.\n1062:     Drop,\n1063: }\n1064: \n1065: /// Kind of access to a value: read or write\n1066: /// (For informational purposes only)\n1067: #[derive(Copy, Clone, PartialEq, Eq, Debug)]\n1068: enum ReadOrWrite {\n1069:     /// From the RFC: \"A *read* means that the existing data may be\n1070:     /// read, but will not be changed.\"\n1071:     Read(ReadKind),\n1072: \n1073:     /// From the RFC: \"A Write(WriteKind),\n1077: \n1078:     /// For two-phase borrows, we distinguish a reservation (which is treated\n1079:     /// like a Read) from an activation (which is treated like a write), Kind of read access to a value\n1086: /// (For informational purposes only)\n1087: #[derive(Copy, Clone, PartialEq, Eq, Debug)]\n1088: enum ReadKind {\n1089:     Borrow(BorrowKind),\n1090: StorageDeadOrDrop,\n1098:     Replace,\n1099:     MutableBorrow(BorrowKind),\n1100:     Mutate,\n1101:     Move,\n1102: }\n1103: \n1104: /// When checking permissions for a place access, this flag is \n1168: impl<'a, 'tcx> MirBorrowckCtxt<'a, '_, 'tcx> {\n1169:     fn body(&self) -> &'a Body<'tcx> {\n1170:         self.body\n1171:     }\n1172: \n1173:     /// Checks an access to the given place to Examines the set of borrows\n1174:     /// that are in scope, as well as which paths have been initialized, to ensure that (a) the\n1175:     /// place is initialized and (b) it is not borrowed in some way that would prevent this\n1176:     /// access.\n1177:     ///\n1178:     /// Returns `true` if an error is reported.\n1179:     fn access_place(\n1180:         &mut self,\n1181:         location: Location,\n1182:         place_span: (Place<'tcx>, Span),\n1183:         kind: (AccessDepth, ReadOrWrite),\n1184:         is_local_mutation_allowed: LocalMutationIsAllowed,\n1185:         state: &BorrowckDomain,\n1186:     ) {\n1187:         let (sd, rw) = kind;\n1188: \n1189:         if let Activation(_, borrow_index) = rw {\n1190:             if       \"access_place: suppressing error place_span=`{:?}` kind=`{:?}`\",\n1207:                 place_span, kind\n1208:             );\n1209:             return;\n1210:         }\n1211: \n1212: location,\n1218:         );\n1219:         let conflict_error = self.check_access_for_conflict(location, place_span, sd, rw, state);\n1220: \n1221:         if conflict_error || mutability_error {\n1222:             debug!(\"access_place: logging error place_span=`{:?}` kind=`{:?}`\", place_span, kind);\n1223:             self.access_place_error_reported.insert((place_span.0, place_span.1));\n1224:         }\n1225:     }\n1226: \n1227:     fn borrows_in_scope<'s>(\n1228:         &self,\n1229:         location: Location,\n1230:         state: &'s BorrowckDomain,\n1231:     ) -> Cow<'s, MixedBitSet<BorrowIndex>> {\n1232:         if let Some(polonius) = &self.polonius_output {\n1233:             // Use polonius output if it has been enabled.\n1234:             let Cow::Borrowed(&state.borrows)\n1242:         }\n1243:     }\n1244: \n1245:     #[instrument(level = \"debug\", skip(self, state))]\n1246:     fn check_access_for_conflict(\n1247:         &mut self,\n1248:         location: Location,\n1249:         place_span: (Place<'tcx>, Span),\n1250:         sd: AccessDepth,\n1251:         rw: ReadOrWrite,\n1252:         state: &BorrowckDomain,\n1253:     ) -> bool {\n1254:         let mut error_reported = false;\n1255: \n1256:         let borrows_in_scope = self.borrows_in_scope(location, state);\n1257: \n1258:         each_borrow_involving_path(\n1259:             self,\n1260:             self.infcx.tcx,\n1261:             self.body,\n1262:             (sd, place_span.0),\n1263:             self.borrow_set,\n1264:             |borrow_index| borrows_in_scope.contains(borrow_index),\n1265:             |this, borrow_index, borrow| match (rw, borrow.kind) {\n1266:                 // Obviously an activation is //\n1270:                 // NOTE: *reservations* do conflict with themselves;\n1271:                 // thus aren't injecting unsoundness w/ this check.)\n1272:                 (Activation(_,           (borrow_index, borrow),\n1280:                     );\n1281:                     ControlFlow::Continue(())\n1282:                 }\n1283: \n1284:                 (Read(_), BorrowKind::Mut { .. },\n1288:                 ) => ControlFlow::Continue(()),\n1289: \n1290:                 (Reservation(_), BorrowKind::Fake(_) | BorrowKind::Shared) => {\n1291:                     // This used to be a future compatibility warning (to be\n1292:                     // disallowed on NLL). See rust-lang/rust#56254\n1293:                     ControlFlow::Continue(())\n1294:                 }\n1295: \n1296:                 (Write(WriteKind::Move), BorrowKind::Fake(FakeBorrowKind::Shallow)) => {\n1297:                     // Handled by initialization checks.\n1298:                     ControlFlow::Continue(())\n1299:                 }\n1300: \n1301:                 (Read(kind), BorrowKind::Mut { .. }) => {\n1302:                     // Reading from mere reservations of mutable-borrows is OK.\n1303:                     if               }\n1315:                         ReadKind::Borrow(bk) => {\n1316:                             let err =\n1317:                                 this.report_conflicting_borrow(location,                  }\n1334:                         Activation(_, activating) => {\n1335:                             debug!(\n1336:                                 \"observing check_place for                  WriteKind::MutableBorrow(bk) => {\n1347:                             let err =\n1348:                                 this.report_conflicting_borrow(location, place_span, bk,      }\n1370:             },\n1371:         );\n1372: \n1373:         error_reported\n1374:     }\n1375: \n1376:     /// Through #123739, `BackwardIncompatibleDropHint`s (BIDs) are introduced.\n1377:     /// We would like to emit lints whether borrow checking fails at these future drop locations.\n1378:     #[instrument(level = \"debug\", skip(self, state))]\n1379:     fn check_backward_incompatible_drop(\n1380:         &mut self,\n1381:         location: Location,\n1382:         place: Place<'tcx>,\n1383:         state: &BorrowckDomain,\n1384:     ) {\n1385: locals,\n1388:         // and we'll ICE because we don't track borrows behind shared references.\n1389:         let sd = if place.ty(self.body, tcx).ty.needs_drop(tcx, self.body.typing_env(tcx))            (sd, place),\n1404:             self.borrow_set,\n1405:             |borrow_index| borrows_in_scope.contains(borrow_index),\n1406:             |this, _borrow_index, borrow| {\n1407: },\n1424:                 );\n1425:                 // We may stop at the first case\n1426:                 ControlFlow::Break(())\n1427:             },\n1428:         );\n1429:     }\n1430: \n1431:     fn mutate_place(\n1432:         &mut self,\n1433:         location: Location,\n1434:         place_span: (Place<'tcx>, Span),\n1435:         kind: AccessDepth,\n1436:         state:      state: &BorrowckDomain,\n1455:     ) {\n1456:         match rvalue {\n1457:             &Rvalue::Ref(_ /*rgn*/, bk, place) => {\n1458:                 let access_kind = match bk {\n1459: We are modifying something through a mut-ref\n1607:             // b. We are modifying something that is local to our parent\n1608:             // c. Current body is a nested closure, and we are modifying path starting from\n1609:             //    a Place captured by our parent closure.\n1610: \n1611:             // Handle (c), the path being modified is exactly the path captured by our parent\n1612:             if let Some(field) = this.is_upvar_field_projection(place.as_ref()) {\n1613:                 this.used_mut_upvars.push(field);\n1614:                 return;\n1615:             }\n1616: \n1617:             for (place_ref, proj) in place.iter_projections().rev() {\n1618:                 //     // when generating MIR.\n1642:         match *operand {\n1643:             Operand::Move(place) | Operand::Copy(place) => {\n1644:                 match place.as_local() {\n1645: variable will be marked as mutable by the borrow.\n1648:                             return;\n1649:                         }\n1650:                         // This is an edge case where we have a             // closure from a shared reference.\n1661:                         //\n1662:                         // As such we have to search for the local that this\n1663:                         // {}\n1703:         }\n1704:     }\n1705: \n1706:     fn consume_operand(\n1707:         &mut self,\n1708:         location: Location,\n1709:         (operand, span): (&Operand<'tcx>, Span),\n1710: #[instrument(level = \"debug\", skip(self))]\n1760:     fn check_for_invalidation_at_exit(\n1761:         &mut self,\n1762:         location: Location,\n1763:         borrow: &BorrowData<'tcx>,\n1764: support: For each activation that is newly\n1825:         // generated at this statement, check if it interferes with\n1826:         // another borrow.\n1827:         for &borrow_index in check_movable_place(&mut self, location: Location, place: Place<'tcx>) {\n1850:         use IllegalMoveOriginKind::*;\n1851: \n1852:         let body = self.body;\n1853:         let tcx =             | ty::Uint(_)\n1877:                     | ty::Float(_)\n1878:                     | ty::Foreign(_)\n1879:                     | ty::Str\n1880:                     | ty::Array(_, _)\n1881:                     | ty::Pat(_, _)\n1882:                     | ty::Slice(_)\n1883:                     | ty::FnDef(_, _)\n1884:                     | ty::FnPtr(..)\n1885:                     | ty::Dynamic(_, _)\n1886:                     | ty::Closure(_, _)\n1887:                     | ty::CoroutineClosure(_, _)\n1888:                     | ty::Coroutine(_, _)\n1889:                     | self.move_errors.push(MoveError::new(\n1906:                                 place,\n1907:                                 location,\n1908:                                 InteriorOfTypeWithDestructor         | ty::RawPtr(_, _)\n1928:                     | ty::Ref(_, _, _)\n1929:                     | ty::FnDef(_, _)\n1930:                     | ty::FnPtr(..)\n1931:                     |               ProjectionElem::Index(_) => match place_ty.ty.kind() {\n1959:                     ty::Array(..) | ty::Slice(..) => {\n1960: place_ty.ty, is_index: true },\n1964:                         ));\n1965:                         return;\n1966:                     }\n1967:                     _ => bug!(\"Unexpected type {place_ty:#?}\"),\n1968:                 },\n1969:                 // `OpaqueCast`: only transmutes the type, so no moves there.\n1970:                 // `Downcast`  : only changes information about a `Place` without moving.\n1971:                 // So it's safe to skip these.\n1972:                 ProjectionElem::OpaqueCast(_)\n1973:                 | ProjectionElem::Downcast(_, _)\n1974:                 | ProjectionElem::UnwrapUnsafeBinder(_) => (),\n1975:             }\n1976: \n1977:             place_ty = place_ty.projection_ty(tcx, elem);\n1978:         }\n1979:     }\n1980: \n1981:     fn check_if_full_path_is_moved(\n1982:         &mut self,\n1983:         location: Location,\n1984:         desired_action: InitializationRequiringAction,\n1985:         place_span: (PlaceRef<'tcx>, Span),\n1986:         state: &BorrowckDomain,\n1987:     ) {\n1988:         let maybe_uninits = &state.uninits;\n1989: \n1990:         // Bad scenarios:\n1991:         //\n1992:         // 1. Move of `a.b.c`, use of `a.b.c`\n1993:         // 2. Move of `a.b.c`, use of `a.b.c.d` (without first reinitializing `a.b.c.d`)\n1994:         // 3. Uninitialized `(a.b.c: &_)`, use of `*a.b.c`; note that with\n1995:         //    partial initialization support, one might have `a.x`\n1996:         //    initialized but not `a.b`.\n1997:         //\n1998:         // OK scenarios:\n1999:         //\n2000:         // 4. Move of `a.b.c`, use of `a.b.d`\n2001:         // 5. Uninitialized `a.x`, initialized `a.b`, use of `a.b`\n2002:         // 6. Copied `(a.b: &_)`, use of `*(a.b).c`; note that `a.b`\n2003:         //    must have been initialized for the use to be sound.\n2004:         // 7. Move of `a.b.c` then reinit of `a.b.c.d`, use of `a.b.c.d`\n2005: \n2006:         // The dataflow tracks shallow prefixes distinctly (that is,\n2007:         // field-accesses on P distinctly from P itself), in order to\n2008:         // track substructure initialization separately from the whole\n2009:         // structure.\n2010:         //\n2011:         // E.g., when looking at (*a.b.c).d, if the closest prefix for\n2012:         // which we have a MovePath is `a.b`, then that means that the\n2013:         // initialization state of `a.b` is all we need to inspect to\n2014:         // know if `a.b.c` is valid (and from that we infer that the\n2015:         // dereference and `.d` access is also valid, since we assume\n2016:         // `a.b.c` is assigned a reference to an initialized and\n2017:         // well-formed record structure.)\n2018: \n2019:         // Therefore, if we seek out the *closest* prefix for which we\n2020:         // have a MovePath, that should capture the initialization\n2021:         // state for the place scenario.\n2022:         //\n2023:         // This code covers scenarios 1, 2, and 3.\n2024: \n2025:         debug!(\"check_if_full_path_is_moved place: {:?}\", place_span.0);\n2026:         let (prefix, mpi) = self.move_path_closest_to(place_span.0);\n2027:         if maybe_uninits.contains(mpi) {\n2028:             self.report_use_of_moved_or_uninitialized(\n2029:                 location,\n2030:                 desired_action,\n2031:                 (prefix, place_span.0, place_span.1),\n2032:                 mpi,\n2033:             );\n2034:         } // Only query longest prefix with a MovePath, not further\n2035:         // ancestors; dataflow recurs on children when parents\n2036:         // move (to support partial (re)inits).\n2037:         //\n2038:         // (I.e., querying parents breaks scenario 7; but may want\n2039:         // to do such a query based on partial-init feature-gate.)\n2040:     }\n2041: \n2042:     /// Subslices correspond to multiple move paths, so we iterate through the\n2043:     /// elements of the base array. For each element we check\n2044:     ///\n2045:     /// * Does this element overlap with our slice.\n2046:     /// * Is any part of it uninitialized.\n2047:     fn check_if_subslice_element_is_moved(\n2048:         &mut self,\n2049:         location: Location,\n2050:         desired_action: InitializationRequiringAction,\n2051:         place_span: (PlaceRef<'tcx>, Span),\n2052:         maybe_uninits: &MixedBitSet<MovePathIndex>,\n2053:         from: u64,\n2054:         to: u64,\n2055:     ) {\n2056:         if let Some(mpi) = self.move_path_for_place(place_span.0) {\n2057:             let move_paths = &self.move_data.move_paths;\n2058: \n2059:             let root_path = &move_paths[mpi];\n2060:             for (child_mpi, child_move_path) in root_path.children(move_paths) {\n2061:                 let last_proj = child_move_path.place.projection.last().unwrap();\n2062:                 if let ProjectionElem::ConstantIndex { offset, from_end, .. } = last_proj {\n2063:                     debug_assert!(!from_end, \"Array constant indexing shouldn't be `from_end`.\");\n2064: \n2065:                     if (from..to).contains(offset) {\n2066:                         let uninit_child =\n2067:                             self.move_data.find_in_move_path_or_its_descendants(child_mpi, |mpi| {\n2068:                                 maybe_uninits.contains(mpi)\n2069:                             });\n2070: \n2071:                         if let Some(uninit_child) = uninit_child {\n2072:                             self.report_use_of_moved_or_uninitialized(\n2073:                                 location,\n2074:                                 desired_action,\n2075:                                 (place_span.0, place_span.0, place_span.1),\n2076:                                 uninit_child,\n2077:                             );\n2078:                             return; // don't bother finding other problems.\n2079:                         }\n2080:                     }\n2081:                 }\n2082:             }\n2083:         }\n2084:     }\n2085: \n2086:     fn check_if_path_or_subpath_is_moved(\n2087:         &mut self,\n2088:         location: Location,\n2089:         desired_action: InitializationRequiringAction,\n2090:         place_span: (PlaceRef<'tcx>, Span),\n2091:         state: &BorrowckDomain,\n2092:     ) {\n2093:         let maybe_uninits = &state.uninits;\n2094: \n2095:         // Bad scenarios:\n2096:         //\n2097:         // 1. Move of `a.b.c`, use of `a` or `a.b`\n2098:         //    partial initialization support, one might have `a.x`\n2099:         //    initialized but not `a.b`.\n2100:         // 2. All bad scenarios from `check_if_full_path_is_moved`\n2101:         //\n2102:         // OK scenarios:\n2103:         //\n2104:         // 3. Move of `a.b.c`, use of `a.b.d`\n2105:         // 4. Uninitialized `a.x`, initialized `a.b`, use of `a.b`\n2106:         // 5. Copied `(a.b: &_)`, use of `*(a.b).c`; note that `a.b`\n2107:         //    must have been initialized for the use to be sound.\n2108:         // 6. Move of `a.b.c` then reinit of `a.b.c.d`, use of `a.b.c.d`\n2109: \n2110:         self.check_if_full_path_is_moved(location, desired_action, place_span, state);\n2111: \n2112:         if let Some((place_base, ProjectionElem::Subslice { from, to, from_end: false })) =\n2113:             place_span.0.last_projection()\n2114:         {\n2115:             let place_ty = place_base.ty(self.body(), self.infcx.tcx);\n2116:             if let ty::Array(..) = place_ty.ty.kind() {\n2117:                 self.check_if_subslice_element_is_moved(\n2118:                     location,\n2119:                     desired_action,\n2120:                     (place_base, place_span.1),\n2121:                     maybe_uninits,\n2122:                     from,\n2123:                     to,\n2124:                 );\n2125:                 return;\n2126:             }\n2127:         }\n2128: \n2129:         // A move of any shallow suffix of `place` also interferes\n2130:         // with an attempt to use `place`. This is scenario 3 above.\n2131:         //\n2132:         // (Distinct from handling of scenarios 1+2+4 above because\n2133:         // `place` does not interfere with suffixes of its prefixes,\n2134:         // e.g., `a.b.c` does not interfere with `a.b.d`)\n2135:         //\n2136:         // This code covers scenario 1.\n2137: \n2138:         debug!(\"check_if_path_or_subpath_is_moved place: {:?}\", place_span.0);\n2139:         if let Some(mpi) = self.move_path_for_place(place_span.0) {\n2140:             let uninit_mpi = self\n2141:                 .move_data\n2142:                 .find_in_move_path_or_its_descendants(mpi, |mpi| maybe_uninits.contains(mpi));\n2143: \n2144:             if let Some(uninit_mpi) = uninit_mpi {\n2145:                 self.report_use_of_moved_or_uninitialized(\n2146:                     location,\n2147:                     desired_action,\n2148:                     (place_span.0, place_span.0, place_span.1),\n2149:                     uninit_mpi,\n2150:                 );\n2151:                 return; // don't bother finding other problems.\n2152:             }\n2153:         }\n2154:     }\n2155: \n2156:     /// Currently MoveData does not store entries for all places in\n2157:     /// the input MIR. For example it will currently filter out\n2158:     /// places that are Copy; thus we do not track places of shared\n2159:     /// reference type. This routine will walk up a place along its\n2160:     /// prefixes, searching for a foundational place that *is*\n2161:     /// tracked in the MoveData.\n2162:     ///\n2163:     /// An Err result includes a tag indicated why the search failed.\n2164:     /// Currently this can only occur if the place is built off of a\n2165:     /// static variable, as we do not track those in the MoveData.\n2166:     fn move_path_closest_to(&mut self, place: PlaceRef<'tcx>) -> (PlaceRef<'tcx>, MovePathIndex) {\n2167:         match self.move_data.rev_lookup.find(place) {\n2168:             LookupResult::Parent(Some(mpi)) | LookupResult::Exact(mpi) => {\n2169:                 (self.move_data.move_paths[mpi].place.as_ref(), mpi)\n2170:             }\n2171:             LookupResult::Parent(None) => panic!(\"should have move path for every Local\"),\n2172:         }\n2173:     }\n2174: \n2175:     fn move_path_for_place(&mut self, place: PlaceRef<'tcx>) -> Option<MovePathIndex> {\n2176:         // If returns None, then there is no move path corresponding\n2177:         // to a direct owner of `place` (which means there is nothing\n2178:         // that borrowck tracks for its analysis).\n2179: \n2180:         match self.move_data.rev_lookup.find(place) {\n2181:             LookupResult::Parent(_) => None,\n2182:             LookupResult::Exact(mpi) => Some(mpi),\n2183:         }\n2184:     }\n2185: \n2186:     fn check_if_assigned_path_is_moved(\n2187:         &mut self,\n2188:         location: Location,\n2189:         (place, span): (Place<'tcx>, Span),\n2190:         state: &BorrowckDomain,\n2191:     ) {\n2192:         debug!(\"check_if_assigned_path_is_moved place: {:?}\", place);\n2193: \n2194:         // None case => assigning to `x` does not require `x` be initialized.\n2195:         for (place_base, elem) in place.iter_projections().rev() {\n2196:             match elem {\n2197:                 ProjectionElem::Index(_/*operand*/) |\n2198:                 ProjectionElem::OpaqueCast(_) |\n2199:                 ProjectionElem::ConstantIndex { .. } |\n2200:                 // assigning to P[i] requires P to be valid.\n2201:                 ProjectionElem::Downcast(_/*adt_def*/, _/*variant_idx*/) =>\n2202:                 // assigning to (P->variant) is okay if assigning to `P` is okay\n2203:                 //\n2204:                 // FIXME: is this true even if P is an adt with a dtor?\n2205:                 { }\n2206: \n2207:                 ProjectionElem::UnwrapUnsafeBinder(_) => {\n2208:                     check_parent_of_field(self, location, place_base, span, state);\n2209:                 }\n2210: \n2211:                 // assigning to (*P) requires P to be initialized\n2212:                 ProjectionElem::Deref => {\n2213:                     self.check_if_full_path_is_moved(\n2214:                         location, InitializationRequiringAction::Use,\n2215:                         (place_base, span), state);\n2216:                     // (base initialized; no need to\n2217:                     // recur further)\n2218:                     break;\n2219:                 }\n2220: \n2221:                 ProjectionElem::Subslice { .. } => {\n2222:                     panic!(\"we don't allow assignments to subslices, location: {location:?}\");\n2223:                 }\n2224: \n2225:                 ProjectionElem::Field(..) => {\n2226:                     // if type of `P` has a dtor, then\n2227:                     // assigning to `P.f` requires `P` itself\n2228:                     // be already initialized\n2229:                     let tcx = self.infcx.tcx;\n2230:                     let base_ty = place_base.ty(self.body(), tcx).ty;\n2231:                     match base_ty.kind() {\n2232:                         ty::Adt(def, _) if def.has_dtor(tcx) => {\n2233:                             self.check_if_path_or_subpath_is_moved(\n2234:                                 location, InitializationRequiringAction::Assignment,\n2235:                                 (place_base, span), state);\n2236: \n2237:                             // (base initialized; no need to\n2238:                             // recur further)\n2239:                             break;\n2240:                         }\n2241: \n2242:                         // Once `let s; s.x = V; read(s.x);`,\n2243:                         // is allowed, remove this match arm.\n2244:                         ty::Adt(..) | ty::Tuple(..) => {\n2245:                             check_parent_of_field(self, location, place_base, span, state);\n2246:                         }\n2247: \n2248:                         _ => {}\n2249:                     }\n2250:                 }\n2251:             }\n2252:         }\n2253: \n2254:         fn check_parent_of_field<'a, 'tcx>(\n2255:             this: &mut MirBorrowckCtxt<'a, '_, 'tcx>,\n2256:             location: Location,\n2257:             base: PlaceRef<'tcx>,\n2258:             span: Span,\n2259:             state: &BorrowckDomain,\n2260:         ) {\n2261:             // rust-lang/rust#21232: Until Rust allows reads from the\n2262:             // initialized parts of partially initialized structs, we\n2263:             // will, starting with the 2018 edition, reject attempts\n2264:             // to write to structs that are not fully initialized.\n2265:             //\n2266:             // In other words, *until* we allow this:\n2267:             //\n2268:             // 1. `let mut s; s.x = Val; read(s.x);`\n2269:             //\n2270:             // we will for now disallow this:\n2271:             //\n2272:             // 2. `let mut s; s.x = Val;`\n2273:             //\n2274:             // and also this:\n2275:             //\n2276:             // 3. `let mut s = ...; drop(s); s.x=Val;`\n2277:             //\n2278:             // This does not use check_if_path_or_subpath_is_moved,\n2279:             // because we want to *allow* reinitializations of fields:\n2280:             // e.g., want to allow\n2281:             //\n2282:             // `let mut s = ...; drop(s.x); s.x=Val;`\n2283:             //\n2284:             // This does not use check_if_full_path_is_moved on\n2285:             // `base`, because that would report an error about the\n2286:             // `base` as a whole, but in this scenario we *really*\n2287:             // want to report an error about the actual thing that was\n2288:             // moved, which may be some prefix of `base`.\n2289: \n2290:             // Shallow so that we'll stop at any dereference; we'll\n2291:             // report errors about issues with such bases elsewhere.\n2292:             let maybe_uninits = &state.uninits;\n2293: \n2294:             // Find the shortest uninitialized prefix you can reach\n2295:             // without going over a Deref.\n2296:             let mut shortest_uninit_seen = None;\n2297:             for prefix in this.prefixes(base, PrefixSet::Shallow) {\n2298:                 let Some(mpi) = this.move_path_for_place(prefix) else { continue };\n2299: \n2300:                 if maybe_uninits.contains(mpi) {\n2301:                     debug!(\n2302:                         \"check_parent_of_field updating shortest_uninit_seen from {:?} to {:?}\",\n2303:                         shortest_uninit_seen,\n2304:                         Some((prefix, mpi))\n2305:                     );\n2306:                     shortest_uninit_seen = Some((prefix, mpi));\n2307:                 } else {\n2308:                     debug!(\"check_parent_of_field {:?} is definitely initialized\", (prefix, mpi));\n2309:                 }\n2310:             }\n2311: \n2312:             if let Some((prefix, mpi)) = shortest_uninit_seen {\n2313:                 // Check for a reassignment into an uninitialized field of a union (for example,\n2314:                 // after a move out). In this case, do not report an error here. There is an\n2315:                 // exception, if this is the first assignment into the union (that is, there is\n2316:                 // no move out from an earlier location) then this is an attempt at initialization\n2317:                 // of the union - we should error in that case.\n2318:                 let tcx = this.infcx.tcx;\n2319:                 if base.ty(this.body(), tcx).ty.is_union()\n2320:                     && this.move_data.path_map[mpi].iter().any(|moi| {\n2321:                         this.move_data.moves[*moi].source.is_predecessor_of(location, this.body)\n2322:                     })\n2323:                 {\n2324:                     return;\n2325:                 }\n2326: \n2327:                 this.report_use_of_moved_or_uninitialized(\n2328:                     location,\n2329:                     InitializationRequiringAction::PartialAssignment,\n2330:                     (prefix, base, span),\n2331:                     mpi,\n2332:                 );\n2333: \n2334:                 // rust-lang/rust#21232, #54499, #54986: during period where we reject\n2335:                 // partial initialization, do not complain about unnecessary `mut` on\n2336:                 // an attempt to do a partial initialization.\n2337:                 this.used_mut.insert(base.local);\n2338:             }\n2339:         }\n2340:     }\n2341: \n2342:     /// Checks the permissions for the given place and read or write kind\n2343:     ///\n2344:     /// Returns `true` if an error is reported.\n2345:     fn check_access_permissions(\n2346:         &mut self,\n2347:         (place, span): (Place<'tcx>, Span),\n2348:         kind: ReadOrWrite,\n2349:         is_local_mutation_allowed: LocalMutationIsAllowed,\n2350:         state: &BorrowckDomain,\n2351:         location: Location,\n2352:     ) -> bool {\n2353:         debug!(\n2354:             \"check_access_permissions({:?}, {:?}, is_local_mutation_allowed: {:?})\",\n2355:             place, kind, is_local_mutation_allowed\n2356:         );\n2357: \n2358:         let error_access;\n2359:         let the_place_err;\n2360: \n2361:         match kind {\n2362:             Reservation(WriteKind::MutableBorrow(BorrowKind::Mut { kind: mut_borrow_kind }))\n2363:             | Write(WriteKind::MutableBorrow(BorrowKind::Mut { kind: mut_borrow_kind })) => {\n2364:                 let is_local_mutation_allowed = match mut_borrow_kind {\n2365:                     // `ClosureCapture` is used for mutable variable with an immutable binding.\n2366:                     // This is only behaviour difference between `ClosureCapture` and mutable\n2367:                     // borrows.\n2368:                     MutBorrowKind::ClosureCapture => LocalMutationIsAllowed::Yes,\n2369:                     MutBorrowKind::Default | MutBorrowKind::TwoPhaseBorrow => {\n2370:                         is_local_mutation_allowed\n2371:                     }\n2372:                 };\n2373:                 match self.is_mutable(place.as_ref(), is_local_mutation_allowed) {\n2374:                     Ok(root_place) => {\n2375:                         self.add_used_mut(root_place, state);\n2376:                         return false;\n2377:                     }\n2378:                     Err(place_err) => {\n2379:                         error_access = AccessKind::MutableBorrow;\n2380:                         the_place_err = place_err;\n2381:                     }\n2382:                 }\n2383:             }\n2384:             Reservation(WriteKind::Mutate) | Write(WriteKind::Mutate) => {\n2385:                 match self.is_mutable(place.as_ref(), is_local_mutation_allowed) {\n2386:                     Ok(root_place) => {\n2387:                         self.add_used_mut(root_place, state);\n2388:                         return false;\n2389:                     }\n2390:                     Err(place_err) => {\n2391:                         error_access = AccessKind::Mutate;\n2392:                         the_place_err = place_err;\n2393:                     }\n2394:                 }\n2395:             }\n2396: \n2397:             Reservation(\n2398:                 WriteKind::Move\n2399:                 | WriteKind::Replace\n2400:                 | WriteKind::StorageDeadOrDrop\n2401:                 | WriteKind::MutableBorrow(BorrowKind::Shared)\n2402:                 | WriteKind::MutableBorrow(BorrowKind::Fake(_)),\n2403:             )\n2404:             | Write(\n2405:                 WriteKind::Move\n2406:                 | WriteKind::Replace\n2407:                 | WriteKind::StorageDeadOrDrop\n2408:                 | WriteKind::MutableBorrow(BorrowKind::Shared)\n2409:                 | WriteKind::MutableBorrow(BorrowKind::Fake(_)),\n2410:             ) => {\n2411:                 if self.is_mutable(place.as_ref(), is_local_mutation_allowed).is_err()\n2412:                     && !self.has_buffered_diags()\n2413:                 {\n2414:                     // rust-lang/rust#46908: In pure NLL mode this code path should be\n2415:                     // unreachable, but we use `span_delayed_bug` because we can hit this when\n2416:                     // dereferencing a non-Copy raw pointer *and* have `-Ztreat-err-as-bug`\n2417:                     // enabled. The 0th\\n157: /// region refers to `'static`; subsequent region vids refer to the free\\n158: /// regions that appear in the closure (or coroutine's) type, in order of\\n159: /// appearance. Note the free regions in the\\n162: /// closure's signature and captures are erased.\\n163: ///\\n164: /// Example: If type check produces a closure with the closure args:\\n165: ///\\n166: /// ```text\\n167: /// ClosureArgs = [\\n168: ///     'a,                                         // From the parent.\\n169: ///     'b,\\n170: ///     i8,                                         // the \\\"closure kind\\\"\\n171: ///     for<'x> fn(&'<erased> &'x u32) -> &'x u32,  // the \\\"closure signature\\\"\\n172: ///     &'<erased> String,                          // some upvar\\n173: /// ]\\n174: /// ```\\n175: ///\\n176: /// We would \\\"renumber\\\" each free region to a unique vid, as follows:\\n177: ///\\n178: /// ```text\\n179: /// ClosureArgs = [\\n180: ///     '1,                                         // From the parent.\\n181: ///     '2,\\n182: ///     i8,                                         // the \\\"closure kind\\\"\\n183: ///     for<'x> fn(&'3 &'x u32) -> &'x u32,         // the \\\"closure signature\\\"\\n184: ///     &'4 String,                                 // some upvar\\n185: /// ]\\n186: /// ```\\n187: ///\\n188: /// Now the code might impose a requirement like `'1: '2`. When an\n189: /// instance of the closure is created, the corresponding free regions\n190: /// can be extracted from its type and constrained to have the given\n191: /// outlives relationship.\n192: #[derive(Clone, Debug)]\n193: pub struct ClosureRegionRequirements<'tcx> {\n194:     /// The number of external regions defined on the closure. In our\n195:     /// example above, it would be 3 -- one for `'static`, then `'1`\n196:     /// and `'2`. This is just used for a sanity check later on, to\n197:     /// make sure that the number of regions we see at the callsite\n198:     /// matches.\n199:     pub num_external_vids: usize,\n200: \n201:     /// Requirements between the various free regions defined in\n202:     /// indices.\n203:     pub outlives_requirements: Vec<ClosureOutlivesRequirement<'tcx>>,\n204: }\n205: \n206: /// Indicates an outlives-constraint between a type or between two\n207: /// free regions declared on the closure.\n208: #[derive(Copy, Clone, Debug)]\n209: pub struct ClosureOutlivesRequirement<'tcx> {\n210:     // This region or type ...\n211:     pub subject: ClosureOutlivesSubject<'tcx>,\n212: \n213:     // ... must outlive this one.\n214:     pub outlived_free_region: ty::RegionVid,\n215: \n216:     // If not, report an error here ...\n217:     pub blame_span: Span,\n218: \n219:     // ... due to this reason.\n220:     pub category: ConstraintCategory<'tcx>,\n221: }\n222: \n223: // Make sure this enum doesn't unintentionally grow\n224: #[cfg(target_pointer_width = \"64\")]\n225: rustc_data_structures::static_assert_size!(ConstraintCategory<'_>, 16);\n226: \n227: /// The subject of a `ClosureOutlivesRequirement` -- that is, the thing\n228: /// that must outlive some region.\n229: #[derive(Copy, Clone, Debug)]\n230: pub enum ClosureOutlivesSubject<'tcx> {\n231:     /// Subject is a type, typically a type parameter, but could also\n232:     /// be a projection. Indicates a requirement like `T: 'a` being\n233:     /// passed to the caller, where the type here is `T`.\n234:     Ty(ClosureOutlivesSubjectTy<'tcx>),\n235: \n236:     /// Subject is a free region from the closure. Indicates a requirement\n237:     /// like `'a: 'b` being passed to the caller; the region here is `'a`.\n238:     Region(ty::RegionVid),\n239: }\n240: \n241: /// Represents a `ty::Ty` for use in [`ClosureOutlivesSubject`].\n242: ///\n243: /// This abstraction is necessary because the type may include `ReVar` regions,\n244: /// which is what we use internally within NLL code, and they can't be used in\n245: /// a query response.\n246: #[derive(Copy, Clone, Debug)]\n247: pub struct ClosureOutlivesSubjectTy<'tcx> {\n248:     inner: Ty<'tcx>,\n249: }\n250: // DO NOT implement `TypeVisitable` or `TypeFoldable` traits, because this\n251: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/rust--01f6ddf7@525258043d7f9dcc1b69d9abcb9bfea32826a219/-/blob/compiler/rustc_borrowck/src/lib.rs%3FL1-250"}}}

{"type":"user","message":{"role":"user","content":[{"tool_use_id":"toolu_01KuMCGA6B9rSqZ5d1w1oGwK","type":"tool_result","content":"{\"content\":\"1: //! The borrowck rules for proving disjointness are applied from the \\\"root\\\" of the\\n2: //! borrow forwards, iterating over \\\"similar\\\" projections in lockstep until\\n3: //! we can prove overlap one way or another. Essentially, we treat `Overlap` as\\n4: //! a monoid and report a conflict if the product ends up not being `Disjoint`.\\n5: //!\\n6: //! On each step, if we didn't run out of borrow or place, we know that our elements\\n7: //! have the same type, and that they only overlap if they are the identical.\\n8: //!\\n9: //! For example, if we are comparing these:\\n10: //! ```text\\n11: //! BORROW:  (*x1[2].y).z.a\\n12: //! ACCESS:  (*x1[i].y).w.b\\n13: //! ```\\n14: //!\\n15: //! Then our steps are:\\n16: //! ```text\\n17: //!       x1         |   x1          -- places are the same\\n18: //!       x1[2]      |   x1[i]       -- equal or disjoint (disjoint if indexes differ)\\n19: //!       x1[2].y    |   x1[i].y     -- equal or disjoint\\n20: //!      *x1[2].y    |  *x1[i].y     -- equal or disjoint\\n21: //!     (*x1[2].y).z | (*x1[i].y).w  -- we are disjoint and don't need to check more!\\n22: //! ```\\n23: //!\\n24: //! Because `zip` does potentially bad things to the iterator inside, this loop\\n25: //! also handles the case where the access might be a *prefix* of the borrow, e.g.\\n26: //!\\n27: //! ```text\\n28: //! BORROW:  (*x1[2].y).z.a\\n29: //! ACCESS:  x1[i].y\\n30: //! ```\\n31: //!\\n32: //! Then our steps are:\\n33: //! ```text\\n34: //!       x1         |   x1          -- places are the same\\n35: //!       x1[2]      |   x1[i]       -- equal or disjoint (disjoint if indexes differ)\\n36: //!       x1[2].y    |   x1[i].y     -- equal or disjoint\\n37: //! ```\\n38: //!\\n39: //! -- here we run out of access - the borrow can access a part of it. If this\\n40: //! is a full deep access, then we *know* the borrow conflicts with it. However,\\n41: //! if the access is shallow, then we can proceed:\\n42: //!\\n43: //! ```text\\n44: //!       x1[2].y    | (*x1[i].y)    -- a deref! the access can't get past this, so we\\n45: //!                                     are disjoint\\n46: //! ```\\n47: //!\\n48: //! Our invariant is, that at each step of the iteration:\\n49: //!  - If we didn't run out of access to match, our borrow and access are comparable\\n50: //!    and either equal or disjoint.\\n51: //!  - If we did run out of access, the borrow can access a part of it.\\n52: \\n53: use std::cmp::max;\\n54: use std::iter;\\n55: \\n56: use rustc_hir as hir;\\n57: use rustc_middle::bug;\\n58: use rustc_middle::mir::{\\n59:     Body, BorrowKind, FakeBorrowKind, MutBorrowKind, Place, PlaceElem, PlaceRef, ProjectionElem,\\n60: };\\n61: use rustc_middle::ty::{self, TyCtxt};\\n62: use tracing::{debug, instrument};\\n63: \\n64: use crate::{AccessDepth, ArtificialField, Deep, Overlap, Shallow};\\n65: \\n66: /// When checking if a place conflicts with another place, this enum is used to influence decisions\\n67: /// where a place might be equal or disjoint with another place, such as if `a[i] == a[j]`.\\n68: /// `PlaceConflictBias::Overlap` would bias toward assuming that `i` might equal `j` and that these\\n69: /// places overlap. `PlaceConflictBias::NoOverlap` assumes that for the purposes of the predicate\\n70: /// being run in the calling context, the conservative choice is to assume the compared indices\\n71: /// are disjoint (and therefore, do not overlap).\\n72: #[derive(Copy, Clone, Debug, Eq, PartialEq)]\\n73: pub enum PlaceConflictBias {\\n74:     Overlap,\\n75:     NoOverlap,\\n76: }\\n77: \\n78: /// Helper function for checking if places conflict with a mutable borrow and deep access depth.\\n79: /// This is used to check for places conflicting outside of the borrow checking code (such as in\\n80: /// dataflow).\\n81: pub fn places_conflict<'tcx>(\\n82:     tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>,\\n83:     body: &Body<'tcx>,\\n84:     borrow_place: Place<'tcx>,\\n85:     access_place: Place<'tcx>,\\n86:     bias: PlaceConflictBias,\\n87: ) -> bool {\\n88:     borrow_conflicts_with_place(\\n89:         tcx,\\n90:         body,\\n91:         borrow_place,\\n92:         BorrowKind::Mut { kind: MutBorrowKind::TwoPhaseBorrow },\\n93:         access_place.as_ref(),\\n94:         AccessDepth::Deep,\\n95:         bias,\\n96:     )\\n97: }\\n98: \\n99: /// Checks whether the `borrow_place` conflicts with the `access_place` given a borrow kind and\\n100: /// access depth. The `bias` parameter is used to determine how the unknowable (comparing runtime\\n101: /// array indices, for example) should be interpreted - this depends on what the caller wants in\\n102: /// order to make the conservative choice and preserve soundness.\\n103: #[inline]\\n104: pub(super) fn borrow_conflicts_with_place<'tcx>(\\n105:     tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>,\\n106:     body: &Body<'tcx>,\\n107:     borrow_place: Place<'tcx>,\\n108:     borrow_kind: BorrowKind,\\n109:     access_place: PlaceRef<'tcx>,\\n110:     access: AccessDepth,\\n111:     bias: PlaceConflictBias,\\n112: ) -> bool {\\n113:     let borrow_local = borrow_place.local;\\n114:     let access_local = access_place.local;\\n115: \\n116:     if borrow_local != access_local {\\n117:         // We have proven the borrow disjoint - borrow of `a.(...)`, access to `a.(...)`\\n156:         // - borrow of `a.(...)`, access to `b.(...)`\\n157:         //\\n158:         // Here we only see the components we have checked so\\n159:         // far (in our examples, just the first component). We\\n160:         // check whether the components being borrowed vs\\n161:         // accessed are disjoint (as in the second example,\\n162:         // but not the first).\\n163:         match place_projection_conflict(tcx, body, borrow_place, borrow_c, access_c, bias) {\\n164:             Overlap::Arbitrary => {\\n165:                 // We have encountered different fields of potentially\\n166:                 // the same union - the borrow now partially overlaps.\\n167:                 //\\n168:                 // There is no *easy* way of comparing the fields\\n169:                 // further on, because they might have different types\\n170:                 // (e.g., borrows of `u.a.0` and `u.b.y` where `.0` and\\n171:                 // `.y` come from different structs).\\n172:                 //\\n173:                 // We could try to do some things here - e.g., count\\n174:                 // dereferences - but that's probably not a good\\n175:                 // idea, at least for now, so just give up and\\n176:                 // report a conflict. This is unsafe code anyway so\\n177:                 // the user could always use raw pointers.\\n178:                 debug!(\\\"arbitrary -> conflict\\\");\\n179:                 return true;\\n180:             }\\n181:             Overlap::EqualOrDisjoint => {\\n182:                 // This is the recursive case - proceed to the next element.\\n183:             }\\n184:             Overlap::Disjoint => {\\n185:                 // We have proven the borrow disjoint - further\\n186:                 // projections will remain disjoint.\\n187:                 debug!(\\\"disjoint\\\");\\n188:                 return false;\\n189:             }\\n190:         }\\n191:     }\\n192: \\n193:     if borrow_place.projection.len() > access_place.projection.len() {\\n194:         for (base, elem) in borrow_place.iter_projections().skip(access_place.projection.len()) {\\n195:             // Borrow path is longer than the access path. Examples:\\n196:             //\\n197:             // - borrow of `a.b.c`, access to `a.b`\\n198:             //\\n199:             // Here, we know that the borrow can access a part of\\n200:             // our place. This is a conflict if that is a part our\\n201:             // access cares about.\\n202: \\n203:             let base_ty = base.ty(body, tcx).ty;\\n204: \\n205:             match (elem, base_ty.kind(), access) {\\n206:                 (_, _, Shallow(Some(ArtificialField::ArrayLength)))\\n207:                 | (_, _, Shallow(Some(ArtificialField::FakeBorrow))) => {\\n208:                     // The array length is like additional fields on the\\n209:                     // type; it does not overlap any existing data there.\\n210:                     // Furthermore, if cannot actually be a prefix of any\\n211:                     // borrowed place (at least in MIR as it is currently.)\\n212:                     //\\n213:                     // e.g., a (mutable) borrow of `a[5]` while we read the\\n214:                     // array length of `a`.\\n215:                     debug!(\\\"borrow_conflicts_with_place: implicit field\\\");\\n216:                     return false;\\n217:                 }\\n218: \\n219:                 (ProjectionElem::Deref, _, Shallow(None)) => {\\n220:                     // e.g., a borrow of `*x.y` while we shallowly access `x.y` or some\\n221:                     // prefix thereof - the shallow access can't touch anything behind\\n222:                     // the pointer.\\n223:                     debug!(\\\"borrow_conflicts_with_place: shallow access behind ptr\\\");\\n224:                     return false;\\n225:                 }\\n226:                 (ProjectionElem::Deref, ty::Ref(_, _, hir::Mutability::Not), _) => {\\n227:                     // Shouldn't be tracked\\n228:                     bug!(\\\"Tracking borrow behind shared reference.\\\");\\n229:                 }\\n230:                 (ProjectionElem::Deref, ty::Ref(_, _, hir::Mutability::Mut), AccessDepth::Drop) => {\\n231:                     // Values behind a mutable reference are not access either by dropping a\\n232:                     // value, or by StorageDead\\n233:                     debug!(\\\"borrow_conflicts_with_place: drop access behind ptr\\\");\\n234:                     return false;\\n235:                 }\\n236: \\n237:                 (ProjectionElem::Field { .. }, ty::Adt(def, _), AccessDepth::Drop) => {\\n238:                     // Drop can read/write arbitrary projections, so places\\n239:                     // conflict regardless of further projections.\\n240:                     if def.has_dtor(tcx) {\\n241:                         return true;\\n242:                     }\\n243:                 }\\n244: \\n245:                 (ProjectionElem::Deref, _, Deep)\\n246:                 | (ProjectionElem::Deref, _, AccessDepth::Drop)\\n247:                 | (ProjectionElem::Field { .. }, _, _)\\n248:                 | (ProjectionElem::Index { .. }, _, _)\\n249:                 | (ProjectionElem::ConstantIndex { .. }, _, _)\\n250:                 | (ProjectionElem::Subslice { .. }, _, _)\\n251:                 | (ProjectionElem::OpaqueCast { .. }, _, _)\\n252:                 | (ProjectionElem::Downcast { .. }, _, _)\\n253:                 | (ProjectionElem::UnwrapUnsafeBinder(_), _, _) => {\\n254:                     // Recursive case. This can still be disjoint on a\\n255:                     // further iteration if this a shallow access and\\n256:                     // there's a deref later on, e.g., a borrow\\n257:                     // of `*x.y` while accessing `x`.\\n258:                 }\\n259:             }\\n260:         }\\n261:     }\\n262: \\n263:     // Borrow path ran out but access path may not\\n264:     // have. Examples:\\n265:     //\\n266:     // - borrow of `a.b`, access to `a.b.c`\\n267:     // - borrow of `a.b`, access to `a.b`\\n268:     //\\n269:     // In the first example, where we didn't run out of\\n270:     // access, the borrow can access all of our place, so we\\n271:     // have a conflict.\\n272:     //\\n273:     // If the second example, where we did, then we still know\\n274:     // that the borrow can access a *part* of our place that\\n275:     // our access cares about, so we still have a conflict.\\n276:     if borrow_kind == BorrowKind::Fake(FakeBorrowKind::Shallow)\\n277:         && borrow_place.projection.len() < access_place.projection.len()\\n278:     {\\n279:         debug!(\\\"borrow_conflicts_with_place: shallow borrow\\\");\\n280:         false\\n281:     } else {\\n282:         debug!(\\\"borrow_conflicts_with_place: full borrow, CONFLICT\\\");\\n283:         true\\n284:     }\\n285: }\\n286: \\n287: // Given that the bases of `elem1` and `elem2` are always either equal\\n288: // or disjoint (and have the same type!), return the overlap situation\\n289: // between `elem1` and `elem2`.\\n290: fn place_projection_conflict<'tcx>(\\n291:     tcx: TyCtxt<'tcx>,\\n292:     body: &Body<'tcx>,\\n293:     pi1: PlaceRef<'tcx>,\\n294:     pi1_elem: PlaceElem<'tcx>,\\n295:     pi2_elem: PlaceElem<'tcx>,\\n296:     bias: PlaceConflictBias,\\n297: ) -> Overlap {\\n298:     match (pi1_elem, pi2_elem) {\\n299:         (ProjectionElem::Deref, ProjectionElem::Deref) => {\\n300:             // derefs (e.g., `*x` vs. `*x`) - recur.\\n301:             debug!(\\\"place_element_conflict: DISJOINT-OR-EQ-DEREF\\\");\\n302:             Overlap::EqualOrDisjoint\\n303:         }\\n304:         (ProjectionElem::OpaqueCast(_), ProjectionElem::OpaqueCast(_)) => {\\n305:             // casts to other types may always conflict irrespective of the type being cast to.\\n306:             debug!(\\\"place_element_conflict: DISJOINT-OR-EQ-OPAQUE\\\");\\n307:             Overlap::EqualOrDisjoint\\n308:         }\\n309:         (ProjectionElem::Field(f1, _), ProjectionElem::Field(f2, _)) => {\\n310:             if f1 == f2 {\\n311:                 // same field (e.g., `a.y` vs. `a.y`) - recur.\\n312:                 debug!(\\\"place_element_conflict: DISJOINT-OR-EQ-FIELD\\\");\\n313:                 Overlap::EqualOrDisjoint\\n314:             } else {\\n315:                 let ty = pi1.ty(body, tcx).ty;\\n316:                 if ty.is_union() {\\n317:                     // Different fields of a union, we are basically stuck.\\n318:                     debug!(\\\"place_element_conflict: STUCK-UNION\\\");\\n319:                     Overlap::Arbitrary\\n320:                 } else {\\n321:                     // Different fields of a struct (`a.x` vs. `a.y`). Disjoint!\\n322:                     debug!(\\\"place_element_conflict: DISJOINT-FIELD\\\");\\n323:                     Overlap::Disjoint\\n324:                 }\\n325:             }\\n326:         }\\n327:         (ProjectionElem::Downcast(_, v1), ProjectionElem::Downcast(_, v2)) => {\\n328:             // different variants are treated as having disjoint fields,\\n329:             // even if they occupy the same \\\"space\\\", because it's\\n330:             // impossible for 2 variants of the same enum to exist\\n331:             // (and therefore, to be borrowed) at the same time.\\n332:             //\\n333:             // Note that this is different from unions - we *do* allow\\n334:             // this code to compile:\\n335:             //\\n336:             // ```\\n337:             // fn foo(x: &mut Result<i32, i32>) {\\n338:             //     let mut v = None;\\n339:             //     if let Ok(ref mut a) = *x {\\n340:             //         v = Some(a);\\n341:             //     }\\n342:             //     // here, you would *think* that the\\n343:             //     // *entirety* of `x` would be borrowed,\\n344:             //     // but in fact only the `Ok` variant is,\\n345:             //     // so the `Err` variant is *entirely free*:\\n346:             //     if let Err(ref mut a) = *x {\\n347:             //         v = Some(a);\\n348:             //     }\\n349:             //     drop(v);\\n350:             // }\\n351:             // ```\\n352:             if v1 == v2 {\\n353:                 debug!(\\\"place_element_conflict: DISJOINT-OR-EQ-FIELD\\\");\\n354:                 Overlap::EqualOrDisjoint\\n355:             } else {\\n356:                 debug!(\\\"place_element_conflict: DISJOINT-FIELD\\\");\\n357:                 Overlap::Disjoint\\n358:             }\\n359:         }\\n360:         (\\n361:             ProjectionElem::Index(..),\\n362:             ProjectionElem::Index(..)\\n363:             | ProjectionElem::ConstantIndex { .. }\\n364:             | ProjectionElem::Subslice { .. },\\n365:         )\\n366:         | (\\n367:             ProjectionElem::ConstantIndex { .. } | ProjectionElem::Subslice { .. },\\n368:             ProjectionElem::Index(..),\\n369:         ) => {\\n370:             // Array indexes (`a[0]` vs. `a[i]`). These can either be disjoint\\n371:             // (if the indexes differ) or equal (if they are the same).\\n372:             match bias {\\n373:                 PlaceConflictBias::Overlap => {\\n374:                     // If we are biased towards overlapping, then this is the recursive\\n375:                     // case that gives \\\"equal *or* disjoint\\\" its meaning.\\n376:                     debug!(\\\"place_element_conflict: DISJOINT-OR-EQ-ARRAY-INDEX\\\");\\n377:                     Overlap::EqualOrDisjoint\\n378:                 }\\n379:                 PlaceConflictBias::NoOverlap => {\\n380:                     // If we are biased towards no overlapping, then this is disjoint.\\n381:                     debug!(\\\"place_element_conflict: DISJOINT-ARRAY-INDEX\\\");\\n382:                     Overlap::Disjoint\\n383:                 }\\n384:             }\\n385:         }\\n386:         (\\n387:             ProjectionElem::ConstantIndex { offset: o1, min_length: _, from_end: false },\\n388:             ProjectionElem::ConstantIndex { offset: o2, min_length: _, from_end: false },\\n389:         )\\n390:         | (\\n391:             ProjectionElem::ConstantIndex { offset: o1, min_length: _, from_end: true },\\n392:             ProjectionElem::ConstantIndex { offset: o2, min_length: _, from_end: true },\\n393:         ) => {\\n394:             if o1 == o2 {\\n395:                 debug!(\\\"place_element_conflict: DISJOINT-OR-EQ-ARRAY-CONSTANT-INDEX\\\");\\n396:                 Overlap::EqualOrDisjoint\\n397:             } else {\\n398:                 debug!(\\\"place_element_conflict: DISJOINT-ARRAY-CONSTANT-INDEX\\\");\\n399:                 Overlap::Disjoint\\n400:             }\\n401:         }\\n402:         (\\n403:             ProjectionElem::ConstantIndex {\\n404:                 offset: offset_from_begin,\\n405:                 min_length: min_length1,\\n406:                 from_end: false,\\n407:             },\\n408:             ProjectionElem::ConstantIndex {\\n409:                 offset: offset_from_end,\\n410:                 min_length: min_length2,\\n411:                 from_end: true,\\n412:             },\\n413:         )\\n414:         | (\\n415:             ProjectionElem::ConstantIndex {\\n416:                 offset: offset_from_end,\\n417:                 min_length: min_length: min_length2,\\n423:                 from_end: false,\\n424:             },\\n425:         ) => {\\n426:             // both patterns matched so it must be at least the greater of the two\\n427:             let min_length = max(min_length1, min_length2);\\n428:             // `offset_from_end` can be in range `[1..min_length]`, 1 indicates the last\\n429:             // element (like -1 in Python) and `min_length` the first.\\n430:             // Therefore, `min_length - offset_from_end` gives the minimal possible\\n431:             // offset from the beginning\\n432:             if offset_from_begin >= min_length - offset_from_end {\\n433:                 debug!(\\\"place_element_conflict: DISJOINT-OR-EQ-ARRAY-CONSTANT-INDEX-FE\\\");\\n434:                 Overlap::EqualOrDisjoint\\n435:             } else {\\n436:                 debug!(\\\"place_element_conflict: DISJOINT-ARRAY-CONSTANT-INDEX-FE\\\");\\n437:                 Overlap::Disjoint\\n438: from_end: false },\\n443:         )\\n444:         | (\\n445:             ProjectionElem::Subslice { from, to, from_end: false },\\n446:             ProjectionElem::ConstantIndex { offset, min_length: _, from_end: false },\\n447:         ) => {\\n448:             if (from..to).contains(&offset) {\\n449:                 debug!(\\\"place_element_conflict: DISJOINT-OR-EQ-ARRAY-CONSTANT-INDEX-SUBSLICE\\\");\\n450:                 Overlap::EqualOrDisjoint\\n451:             } else {\\n452:                 debug!(\\\"place_element_conflict: min_length: _, from_end: false },\\n458:             ProjectionElem::Subslice { from, .. },\\n459:         )\\n460:         | (\\n461:             ProjectionElem::Subslice { from, .. },\\n462: DISJOINT-SLICE-CONSTANT-INDEX-SUBSLICE\\\");\\n469:                 Overlap::Disjoint\\n470:             }\\n471:         }\\n472:         (\\n473:             ProjectionElem::ConstantIndex { offset,                    \\\"place_element_conflict: \\\\\\n483:                        DISJOINT-OR-EQ-SLICE-CONSTANT-INDEX-SUBSLICE-FE\\\"\\n484:                 );\\n485: { from: f2, to: t2, from_end: false },\\n494:         ) => {\\n495:             if f2 >= t1 || f1 >= t2 {\\n496:                 debug!(\\\"place_element_conflict:
